ARIE 1923-1924 [vol. 046]


A.--List of copper plates examined during the year 1923-24.


ARIE/1923-1924/A/1923-24/1 (page 10)
Placement
Sri. L.N.Deb, Jubraj of Tekkali.
Dynasty
Eastern Gaṅga.
King
Indravarman, son of Dānār-ṇava.
Date
(Gaṅga) year 154, Solar Eclipse.
Language
Sanskrit
Origin
Returned to the owner.
Edition
Epigraphia Indica.
Remarks
Registers the grant, by the king, of some lands in the village of Tuṅgannā in the Rūppavati-vishaya as a brahmadēya, to Skandaśarm-man of the Śāṇḍilya-gōtra and the Vājasa-nēya-śākhā, who was learned in the Vēdas and the Vēdāṅgas and who was a resident of (the village) Garakhonna, for the merit of Achchipōḍi-Bhaṭṭārikā. The inscription was composed by the Sarvādhikṛita Śambapurō-pādhyāya, son of Dharmachandra, the Superintendent of Elephants (hastyadhyak-sha) and engraved by Khaṇḍichandra, son of [Ā]ditya-Bhōgaka.
ARIE/1923-1924/A/1923-24/2 (page 10)
Placement
Sri Gopinath Deb, Second Prince of Tekkali.
Dynasty
Do.
King
Dēvēndravarman, son of Rājēn-dravarman.
Date
(Gaṅga) year [11]0.
Language
Sanskrit
Origin
Returned to the owner.
Edition
Epigraphia Indica.
Remarks
Damaged. Registers the grant of the village called Nivi[no] in the [Varāga]vartanī-vishaya, to a poet (name lost) who was the son of Mahāpratīhāra Chandavarmman, by the king, for the merit of his parents. The inscription was composed by Sāmanta Sarva-cha[ndra] and engraved by Sāmanta Khaṇḍi-malla.
ARIE/1923-1924/A/1923-24/3 (page 10)
Placement
The Tahsildar of Tenali
Dynasty
Eastern Chāḷukya.
King
Ammarāja (I) alias Sarvalōkā-śraya Śrī Vishṇuvardhana-Mahārāja.
Date
…
Language
Sanskrit
Origin
Returned to the owner.
Edition
Epigraphia Indica.
Remarks
Damaged. Gives the genealogy and the dura-tions of the reigns of the Eastern Chāḷukya kings down to the king. Registers the grant of the village Pulivaṟṟu in the Velanāṇḍu-vishaya, by the king, to Indaparāja, the grandson of Indaparāja of the Mahāraṭṭa-vaṁśa, who was the ‘lord of the city of Mānyakhēṭa.’
ARIE/1923-1924/A/1923-24/4 (page 10)
Placement
M. R.Ry. K.Nageswara Rao Pantulu Garu, Editor, Andhra Patrika, Madras.
Dynasty
Do.
King
Sakalalōkāśraya Śrī Jayasiṁ-ghavallabha-Mahārāja.
Date
Jyēshṭha, Paurṇamāsī. Saṁkrānti.
Language
Sanskrit
Origin
Returned to the owner.
Edition
…
Remarks
Registers the grant, by the king, of the village Peṇukapaṟu in the Karmarāshṭra to Śrī Eṟa-Drōṇaśarman, who was a resident of Vaṁgipaṟu, who was proficient in the four Vēdas and all the Śāstras, and who was the son of Dēvaśarman who had performed the Sarvakratu sacrifice, and the grandson of Guṁja-Dēvaśarman of the Kauṇḍinya-gōtra, Taittirīya-śākhā and the Āpastamba-sūtra.
ARIE/1923-1924/A/1923-24/5 (page 11)
Placement
M.R.Ry. R.Vaidyanatha Ayyar Avargal, B.A., Deputy Collector, Tirukkoilur, South Arcot district.
Dynasty
…
King
Tribhuvanachakravartin Kōṉēri[ṉ*]maikoṇḍāṉ.
Date
3rd year, Āṉi
Language
Tamil
Origin
Returned to the owner.
Edition
South-Indian Inscriptions.
Remarks
Some plates are missing in the middle. Regis-ters the royal grant of Ulvari, remitting the taxes on shares of land and house-sites, in ratification of the kai-ōlai given to the residents of Avanivēndarāma-chaturvēdi-maṅgalam, which was founded after the king by Aḻagāṇḍār alias Mahābali-Vāṇarā-yar, at Tirunārāyaṇapuram in Vaḍagarai Rājarāja-vaḷanāḍu.
ARIE/1923-1924/A/1923-24/6 (page 11)
Placement
The Tahsildar of Shiyali, Tanjore district.
Dynasty
…
King
…
Date
Chitrabhānu, Makara, [Ardhōdaya ?]
Language
Tamil verse
Origin
Returned to the owner.
Edition
South-Indian Inscriptions.
Remarks
The inscription is engraved on the two sides of a curved copper scimitar with a cup-like depression at the head. Records the gift of a land and a pair of golden eyes to the god Śevvēḷ-Kandaṉ (Subrahmaṇya) at Mayilāḍi, by a commander (Daḷavāy) called Raghu-nātha Śaḍakkattēvaṉ.
ARIE/1923-1924/A/1923-24/7 (page 11)
Placement
Do.
Dynasty
Madura Nāyaka.
King
Śokkaliṅgama-Nāyaka, son of Tirumala-Nāyaka.
Date
Śaka 1595, Pramādīcha, Aṟpaśi 9, śu. Friday, daśamī. Śadaiyam, (Śatabhi-shaj).
Language
Tamil
Origin
Returned to the owner.
Edition
South-Indian Inscriptions.
Remarks
Registers the agreement made, among the residents including the pāḷaiyakārar and the nāṭṭār of the 84 villages in the two māgā-ṇams of Kūttiyapēṭṭai and Pachchaip-peru-mānallūr in Śīgāḻi-sīmai--comprising the tract between the Koḷḷiḍam (Coleroon) and the Kāvērī in Śōḻa-maṇḍalam which is said to have been under the authority of the king --to the effect that they would, on behalf of themselves and the king, collect the maga-mai tax at one nāḻi on every kalam of the produce, for the expenses of the sacred bath and offerings of the goddess Periyanāyaki-Ammaṉ and for repairs in the temple of Tirumēṉi-Aḻagar at Vaḍamayūram alias Tirumayilāḍi.
ARIE/1923-1924/A/1923-24/8 (page 11)
Placement
The Collector of Tanjore
Dynasty
…
King
…
Date
Śaka 1615, Prajōtpatti, Tai 16, Thursday, shashṭhī, Rēvatī.
Language
Tamil
Origin
Returned to the owner.
Edition
South-Indian Inscriptions.
Remarks
Registers the grant, by the residents of several villages, of the right of collecting the magamai tax on the merchandise passing through their villages, to Kumārasvāmi-Tam-birāṉ to meet the expenses of the sacred bath and offerings and repairs in the temple of Vaidyanāthasvāmi, situated in the middle of the two rivers (Ubhaya-Kāvērī, i.e., the Cauvery and the Coleroon) in Rājādhirāja-vaḷanāḍu.
ARIE/1923-1924/A/1923-24/9 (page 12)
Placement
The Collector of Tanjore
Dynasty
Pudukkoṭṭai chiefs.
King
Vijaya Raghunātha Rāya-Bādar (Rai Bahadūr ?) Toṇḍamāṉ.
Date
Śaka 1726, Kali 4905, Raktākshi, Tai 24, chaturthī, śu. Sunday, Uttiraṭṭādi, Śivanāma-yōga, Vaṇik-karaṇa.
Language
Tamil
Origin
Returned to the owner.
Edition
South-Indian Inscriptions.
Remarks
Registers the gift of the village Mudalipaṭṭi alias Vayittinādapuram, which was to remain under the management of Aṭchaya-liṅga-Tambirāṉ of the line of Tirujñāna-sambandha-Dēśika of the Dharmapuram-ādīnam, by the king, for certain daily and special services to the images of Vaidyanātha svāmin and Taiyal Nāyaki-Ammaṉ in the temple at Vaidīśvarankōyil. The names of the Vijayanagara rulers from Mallikārjuna-dēva-Mahārāya down to Śrīraṅgadēva-Mahārāya are indifferently given at the beginning of the inscription.

ARIE/1923-1924/B/1923/224 (page 13)
Placement
On the south wall of the central shrine and the west and south walls of the maṇḍapa of the Sadguṇēśvarasvāmin temple at Karuveli, Nannilam taluk, Tanjore district.
Dynasty
Chōḷa
King
Tribhuvanachakravartin Rājādhirājadēva (II).
Date
4th year
Language
Tamil
Remarks
Damaged. Registers the confirmation, by the Nyāyattār of both the Perundanam and Siṟudanam, of the grants of land, some as Vīrabhōgam, made to the temple of Tiruk-koṭṭiṭṭai-Uḍaiyār at Karuvili alias Kulōttuṅgaśōḻanallūr in Veṇṇāḍu, a subdivision of Uyyakkoṇḍār-vaḷanāḍu, by certain persons at different times in the reign of Kulōttuṅga-Chōḷadēva, “who abolished the tolls.” A certain Pottappichchōḻar figures as one of the donors. Mentions the temple of Paśitāṅgīśvaram-Uḍaiyār.
ARIE/1923-1924/B/1923/225 (page 13)
Placement
On the south wall of the same maṇḍapa.
Dynasty
Do.
King
Tribhuvanachakravar[tin]
Date
8th year
Language
Tamil
Remarks
Damaged. Refers to the 11th year of Rājarājadēva. Records a sale of land to the temple of Paśitāṅgīśvaram-Uḍaiyār at Karuvili by a certain Ārāvamudu Tiruvālavā-yuḍaiyāṉ alias Mattimarāyaṉ in lieu of 100 kāśu which was due from him to the temple. Refers to the grant of some Vīrabhōgam (?) to the members of the Perundanam and Śiṟundanam in the 8th year of the king.

ARIE/1923-1924/B/1923/227 (page 13)
Placement
On a slab lying in the prākāra of the same temple.
Dynasty
…
King
…
Date
Śaka 1642, Chitra-bhānu, Māśi 18.
Language
Tamil
Remarks
Records an undertaking by the residents of the village, that they would conduct the worship and offerings of the god and execute the necessary repairs to the temple out of the produce of the 25 kāṇi of temple land which they had taken over for management, with the additional stipula-tion that they would pay the tax on 5 kāṇi of the land and other plots belonging to the temple.
ARIE/1923-1924/B/1923/228 (page 14)
Placement
On the north, west and south walls of the central shrine in the Matsyapurīśvara temple at Koyil-Tevarayanpettai. hamlet of Pandaravadai, Papanasam taluk, same district.
Dynasty
Chōḷa
King
Rājakēsarivarman alias Vijaya Rājēndra-dēva.
Date
35th year
Language
Tamil
Remarks
Begins with the introduction tigkaLEr taru, etc. Registers an agreement by the big assembly of Rāja-kēsari-chaturvēdimaṅgalam, a brahmadēya in Nallūr-nāḍu, which was a subdivision of Nittavinōda-vaḷanāḍu, to pay all the taxes on a certain land belonging to the temple of Tiruchchēlūr-uḍaiya-Mahādēva in lieu of interest on the money which they had borrowed from the temple-treasury in the 28th year of “Periyadēvar who was pleased to take Pūrvadēśam, Gaṅgai and Kiḍāram” for purchasing house-sites, and in the 31st year of Śrī-Rājādhirājadēva both of which amounts together with their interest had now accumulated to 710 kāśu. Mentions a kaḻañju as equivalent to 2 kāśu.
ARIE/1923-1924/B/1923/229 (page 14)

Do.
King
Parakē[sari]varman alias Rājēndra-Chōḷadēva (I).
Date
7th year
Language
Tamil
Remarks
Begins with the introduction tiruman_n_ivaLara etc. Sale of a house-site to the same princess by a resident of Kalākarachchēri of the village to make up the deficit of the Vaidyabhōga provided (by her) for looking after the hospital called Sundaraśōḻa-Viṇṇagar Ātulaśālai at Tañjāvūr. The Vaidyabhōga gift made by her in the 3rd year of the king and the present gift were to be enjoyed by Savarṇaṉ Araiyaṉ Madurāntakaṉ and his descendents who were natives of Marugal in Marugal-nāḍu, a subdivision of Kshatriyaśikhāmaṇi-vaḷanāḍu. Both these transactions were engraved, it is stated, by the big assembly by order of the princess communicated to them from the palace at Paḻaiyāṟu.

King

Language
Tamil
Remarks
Registers the confiscation of all the property, including a village called Karuvēṟkuṟichchi, houses, gardens, male and female servants, etc., belonging to a certain Āḻiyaṅgaiyaṉ Śattiyanāvaṉ who had killed, with the help of his armed accomplices, one Vāmana-Bhaṭṭa on the night of the 25th of Aṟpaśi while he was returning home from the temple (ambalam), and escaped being caught. The confiscated property was added as a tirunāmattukkāṇi of the temple of Nāyaṉār Śokka-Nārāyaṇa.

Remarks
Registers an agreement by the big assembly of Uttaramēlūr alias Rājēndraśōḻa-chaturvēdimaṅgalam to conduct certain festivals, as of old, in the temple at Tiruppulivanam, and to burn 8 lamps on all the days of the festivals. Of those lamps which were intended to be burnt throughout the year, four were endowed in the 14th year of Rājamāt-tāṇḍaṉ alias Aparājitavikramavarman on the day of a solar-eclipse, one in the 18th year of Kannaradēva ‘who took Kachchi (Conjeeveram) and Tañjai (Tanjore)’, two in the 13th year of Maduraikoṇḍa Parakēsari and one in the 14th year of Tribhuvanavīradēva.

Śaka 14[7]8, Naḷa, Jyēsṭha, śu. 15.
Language
Telugu
Remarks
Records that on the complaint of the villagers, Mahā-maṇḍalēśvara Rāmarāju Viṭṭalarāja Tirumalrājayyadēva-Mahārāja stopped the illegal collections of money on Yeḷahañji, Sōmalāpuram, Untakallu and another village and directed that the fines etc. collected in the village should be utilized for repairing temples, tanks, etc. Dakshiṇāmūrti-Śivāchārya is mentioned as the donee.

C.--Stone inscriptions copied in 1924.


ARIE/1923-1924/C/1924/1 (page 40)

Records the gift of three forehead plates of gold, collected from many sources, by Kāmakkōḍaṉār and also an under-taking by the temple servants to burn two perpetual lamps in the temple, out of the money realized from several sources, in the 26th year of the king. One hundred and eighty sheep were purchased with the latter amount.

Sakalabhuvanachakravartin Kōp-Peruñ-jiṅgadēva.
Date
16th year, Āḍi 30, Sunday.
Language
Tamil
Remarks
Records the non-payment of taxes, due from the 23rd to the 25th year of the king, by a certain person and the subse-quent attachment of his property from his wife and son by bringing up his lands for sale, and the gift of the same for worship, offerings and a lamp in the temple for the welfare of Piḷḷai Śōḻa-Kōṉār.
ARIE/1923-1924/C/1924/433 (page 79)
Placement
On the south wall of the maṇḍapa in front of the same shrine.
Dynasty
Chōḷa
King
Rājakēsarivarman alias Tribhuvana-chakravartin Rājādhirājadēva (II).
Date
8th year
Language
Tamil
Remarks
Begins with the introduction kaTalcUznta pArmAtarum, etc. Mentions the circumstances of the king's coronation through the exertions of a certain Tiruchchiṟṟambala-muḍaiyāṉ Perumānambiyār alias Pallavarāyar, after the death of king Rājarāja (II). Registers the royal grant of 40 vēli of tax free land at Śōḻēndraśiṅga-nallūr in Kurukkai-nāḍu, a subdivision of Virudarājabhayaṅkara-vaḷanāḍu, in some specified proportion, to the relations of Pallavarāyar on his demise. Refers to the campaign of Laṅkāpura-Daṇḍnātha and the refuge offered to Kula-śēkhara by the king against the Ceylonese general.
ARIE/1923-1924/C/1924/434 (page 79)
Placement
On the same wall
Dynasty
Do.
King
Parakēsarivarman alias Tribhuvana-chakravartin Rājarājadēva.
Date
10th year, Siṁha, śu. trayōdaśī, Friday, Tiru-vōṇam.
Language
Tamil
Remarks
Records a sale of land to the temple of Rājarājīśvaram-Uḍaiyār at Kuḷattūr in Tiruvindaḷūr-nāḍu, a subdivision of Rājādhirāja-vaḷanāḍu, by two private individuals of Tiruvindaḷūr.
ARIE/1923-1924/C/1924/435 (page 80)
Placement
On the same wall
Dynasty
Chōḷa
King
Tribhuvanachakravartin Rājarājadēva
Date
10th year
Language
Grantha & Tamil
Remarks
Begins with the introduction pUmaruviya tirumAtum, etc. Records the gift of some lands, as tax-free, for offerings and worship and for a flower-garden to the temple of Rājarājiśvaram-Uḍaiyār at Kuḷattūr by Palla-varāyar mentioned in No. 427 above by whom the temple had also been built.
ARIE/1923-1924/C/1924/436 (page 80)
Placement
Do.
Dynasty
Do.

King
…
Date
Śaka 1438, Dhātu, Uttarāyaṇa, Ṛishabha, śu. trayōdaśī, Wed-nesday, Variha-yōgam, Vyāghra-karaṇa, Svāti.
Language
Tamil
Remarks
Seems to record a gift of land called Alaṅgāravalli by pur-chase, by a certain lady, of Pāttihaśē[ka]ranallūr in Pugaḻiyūr-nāḍu to the temple of Aḻagar at Vāṉavīraṉ-madurai which had been built by her father on the northern bank of the river. Mentions Bhuvanēka-vīraṉ-paṇam and Rāyarvāśil Timmappa-Nāyaka, the administrator of Madura and Sundarattōḷuḍaiyār alias Māvali-Vāṇādarāyar who ‘revived the past.’
